\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\begin{DoxyVerb} This class provides a base class for all sparse arrays.  It
cannot be instantiated.  Most of the work is provided by subclasses.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_acc7b0cddce0de7346efb1ae0c1d8e7f2}\index{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}!\_get\_index\_dtype@{\_get\_index\_dtype}}
\index{\_get\_index\_dtype@{\_get\_index\_dtype}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\_get\_index\_dtype()}{\_get\_index\_dtype()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_acc7b0cddce0de7346efb1ae0c1d8e7f2} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+\_\+get\+\_\+index\+\_\+dtype (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{arrays}{ = {\ttfamily ()}, }\item[{}]{maxval}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{check\+\_\+contents}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Determine index dtype for array.

This wraps _sputils.get_index_dtype, providing compatibility for both
array and matrix API sparse matrices. Matrix API sparse matrices would
attempt to downcast the indices - which can be computationally
expensive and undesirable for users. The array API changes this
behaviour.

See discussion: https://github.com/scipy/scipy/issues/16774

The get_index_dtype import is due to implementation details of the test
suite. It allows the decorator ``with_64bit_maxval_limit`` to mock a
lower int32 max value for checks on the matrix API's downcasting
behaviour.
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{scipy_2sparse_2__base_8py_source_l01269}{1269}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{scipy_2sparse_2__base_8py_source}{\+\_\+base.\+py}}.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_aed88c3614f2e4eddbbce8395e5cc7e51} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+asformat (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{format}{, }\item[{}]{copy}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return this array in the passed format.

Parameters
----------
format : {str, None}
    The desired sparse format ("csr", "csc", "lil", "dok", "array", ...)
    or None for no conversion.
copy : bool, optional
    If True, the result is guaranteed to not share data with self.

Returns
-------
A : This array in the passed format.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a932a2ce1d9ad177fb871ea2cd5f3d3d2}\index{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}!astype@{astype}}
\index{astype@{astype}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{astype()}{astype()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a932a2ce1d9ad177fb871ea2cd5f3d3d2} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+astype (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{dtype}{, }\item[{}]{casting}{ = {\ttfamily \textquotesingle{}unsafe\textquotesingle{}}, }\item[{}]{copy}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Cast the array elements to a specified type.

Parameters
----------
dtype : string or numpy dtype
    Typecode or data-type to which to cast the data.
casting : {'no', 'equiv', 'safe', 'same_kind', 'unsafe'}, optional
    Controls what kind of data casting may occur.
    Defaults to 'unsafe' for backwards compatibility.
    'no' means the data types should not be cast at all.
    'equiv' means only byte-order changes are allowed.
    'safe' means only casts which can preserve values are allowed.
    'same_kind' means only safe casts or casts within a kind,
    like float64 to float32, are allowed.
    'unsafe' means any data conversions may be done.
copy : bool, optional
    If `copy` is `False`, the result might share some memory with this
    array. If `copy` is `True`, it is guaranteed that the result and
    this array do not share any memory.
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented in \mbox{\hyperlink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__data_1_1__data__matrix_a962ce59c1ea73e50ad883228201da493}{scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+data.\+\_\+data\+\_\+matrix}}.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a0731da9574749ac58ec8b6ffb64ed2f0} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+conjugate (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{copy}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Element-wise complex conjugation.

If the array is of non-complex data type and `copy` is False,
this method does nothing and the data is not copied.

Parameters
----------
copy : bool, optional
    If True, the result is guaranteed to not share data with self.

Returns
-------
A : The element-wise complex conjugate.
\end{DoxyVerb}

scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+copy (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Returns a copy of this array.

No data/indices will be shared between the returned value and current
array.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_abd9204e3ccb561e27006e9d735d23ee9}\index{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}!count\_nonzero@{count\_nonzero}}
\index{count\_nonzero@{count\_nonzero}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{count\_nonzero()}{count\_nonzero()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_abd9204e3ccb561e27006e9d735d23ee9} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+count\+\_\+nonzero (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Number of non-zero entries, equivalent to

np.count_nonzero(a.toarray())

Unlike the nnz property, which return the number of stored
entries (the length of the data attribute), this method counts the
actual number of non-zero entries in data.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_adae57c10f4d88f04c6fa7363b4457488}\index{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}!diagonal@{diagonal}}
\index{diagonal@{diagonal}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{diagonal()}{diagonal()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_adae57c10f4d88f04c6fa7363b4457488} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+diagonal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{k}{ = {\ttfamily 0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Returns the kth diagonal of the array.

Parameters
----------
k : int, optional
    Which diagonal to get, corresponding to elements a[i, i+k].
    Default: 0 (the main diagonal).

    .. versionadded:: 1.0

See also
--------
numpy.diagonal : Equivalent numpy function.

Examples
--------
>>> from scipy.sparse import csr_array
>>> A = csr_array([[1, 2, 0], [0, 0, 3], [4, 0, 5]])
>>> A.diagonal()
array([1, 0, 5])
>>> A.diagonal(k=1)
array([2, 3])
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented in \mbox{\hyperlink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__bsr_1_1__bsr__base_a49c1d758fa52af104c5ec01cf92b3579}{scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+bsr.\+\_\+bsr\+\_\+base}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__compressed_1_1__cs__matrix_ab83e1203fcd020d1581143cff865fa54}{scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+compressed.\+\_\+cs\+\_\+matrix}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__coo_1_1__coo__base_a098ccccafd294efb1bf3d0b135368716}{scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+coo.\+\_\+coo\+\_\+base}}, and \mbox{\hyperlink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__dia_1_1__dia__base_aef40c97625e213b3c32741c2947f953e}{scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+dia.\+\_\+dia\+\_\+base}}.

\begin{DoxyVerb}Ordinary dot product

Examples
--------
>>> import numpy as np
>>> from scipy.sparse import csr_array

\end{DoxyVerb}

scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+getnnz (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{axis}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Number of stored values, including explicit zeros.

.. deprecated:: 1.11.0
   This method will be removed in SciPy 1.13.0. Use `X.nnz`
   instead.  The `axis` argument will no longer be supported;
   please let us know if you still need this functionality.

Parameters
----------
axis : None, 0, or 1
    Select between the number of values across the whole array, in
    each column, or in each row.

See also
--------
count_nonzero : Number of non-zero entries
\end{DoxyVerb}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mean()}{mean()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a22be3666a258ee2f297203b8a1da7c73} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+mean (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{axis}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{dtype}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{out}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Compute the arithmetic mean along the specified axis.

Returns the average of the array elements. The average is taken
over all elements in the array by default, otherwise over the
specified axis. `float64` intermediate and return values are used
for integer inputs.

Parameters
----------
axis : {-2, -1, 0, 1, None} optional
    Axis along which the mean is computed. The default is to compute
    the mean of all elements in the array (i.e., `axis` = `None`).
dtype : data-type, optional
    Type to use in computing the mean. For integer inputs, the default
    is `float64`; for floating point inputs, it is the same as the
    input dtype.

    .. versionadded:: 0.18.0

out : np.matrix, optional
    Alternative output matrix in which to place the result. It must
    have the same shape as the expected output, but the type of the
    output values will be cast if necessary.

    .. versionadded:: 0.18.0

Returns
-------
m : np.matrix

See Also
--------
numpy.matrix.mean : NumPy's implementation of 'mean' for matrices
\end{DoxyVerb}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a410c25789e486d0bfd4b014c709dd710} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+multiply (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



NOTE\+: All arithmetic operations use \doxylink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__csr_1_1csr__matrix}{csr\+\_\+matrix} by default. 

Therefore a new sparse array format just needs to define a .\doxylink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_ad6daf64dfe8aa3c4ddc4bc477ab81894}{tocsr()} method to provide arithmetic support. Any of these methods can be overridden for efficiency.

\begin{DoxyVerb}Point-wise multiplication by another array
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented in \mbox{\hyperlink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__compressed_1_1__cs__matrix_a4a8e8f17cd393d3a7bb254a2365e876a}{scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+compressed.\+\_\+cs\+\_\+matrix}}.

\Hypertarget{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a30e0293063cf7541a61a4359b1686648}\index{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}!nonzero@{nonzero}}
\index{nonzero@{nonzero}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{nonzero()}{nonzero()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a30e0293063cf7541a61a4359b1686648} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+nonzero (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}nonzero indices

Returns a tuple of arrays (row,col) containing the indices
of the non-zero elements of the array.

Examples
--------
>>> from scipy.sparse import csr_array
>>> A = csr_array([[1,2,0],[0,0,3],[4,0,5]])
>>> A.nonzero()
(array([0, 0, 1, 2, 2]), array([0, 1, 2, 0, 2]))
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented in \mbox{\hyperlink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__csc_1_1__csc__base_a85ff62c260ffd1ce1f509512714c2122}{scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+csc.\+\_\+csc\+\_\+base}}.

\Hypertarget{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a5830e598c761e841ba6194f6fdd25b0e}\index{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}!reshape@{reshape}}
\index{reshape@{reshape}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{reshape()}{reshape()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a5830e598c761e841ba6194f6fdd25b0e} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+reshape (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{args}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{kwargs}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}reshape(self, shape, order='C', copy=False)

Gives a new shape to a sparse array without changing its data.

Parameters
----------
shape : length-2 tuple of ints
    The new shape should be compatible with the original shape.
order : {'C', 'F'}, optional
    Read the elements using this index order. 'C' means to read and
    write the elements using C-like index order; e.g., read entire first
    row, then second row, etc. 'F' means to read and write the elements
    using Fortran-like index order; e.g., read entire first column, then
    second column, etc.
copy : bool, optional
    Indicates whether or not attributes of self should be copied
    whenever possible. The degree to which attributes are copied varies
    depending on the type of sparse array being used.

Returns
-------
reshaped : sparse array
    A sparse array with the given `shape`, not necessarily of the same
    format as the current object.

See Also
--------
numpy.reshape : NumPy's implementation of 'reshape' for ndarrays
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a3999f9aef96bb5456cc6f78abd190aab}\index{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}!resize@{resize}}
\index{resize@{resize}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{resize()}{resize()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a3999f9aef96bb5456cc6f78abd190aab} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+resize (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{shape}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Resize the array in-place to dimensions given by ``shape``

Any elements that lie within the new shape will remain at the same
indices, while non-zero elements lying outside the new shape are
removed.

Parameters
----------
shape : (int, int)
    number of rows and columns in the new array

Notes
-----
The semantics are not identical to `numpy.ndarray.resize` or
`numpy.resize`. Here, the same data will be maintained at each index
before and after reshape, if that index is within the new bounds. In
numpy, resizing maintains contiguity of the array, moving elements
around in the logical array but not within a flattened representation.

We give no guarantees about whether the underlying data attributes
(arrays, etc.) will be modified in place or replaced with new objects.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a75d9e52d67caabfa35f30ecba49da9fa}\index{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}!setdiag@{setdiag}}
\index{setdiag@{setdiag}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setdiag()}{setdiag()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a75d9e52d67caabfa35f30ecba49da9fa} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+setdiag (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{values}{, }\item[{}]{k}{ = {\ttfamily 0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Set diagonal or off-diagonal elements of the array.

Parameters
----------
values : array_like
    New values of the diagonal elements.

    Values may have any length. If the diagonal is longer than values,
    then the remaining diagonal entries will not be set. If values are
    longer than the diagonal, then the remaining values are ignored.

    If a scalar value is given, all of the diagonal is set to it.

k : int, optional
    Which off-diagonal to set, corresponding to elements a[i,i+k].
    Default: 0 (the main diagonal).
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a8a72a3745c1e28eb9a87998f2e66e826}\index{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}!sum@{sum}}
\index{sum@{sum}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{sum()}{sum()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a8a72a3745c1e28eb9a87998f2e66e826} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+sum (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{axis}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{dtype}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{out}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Sum the array elements over a given axis.

Parameters
----------
axis : {-2, -1, 0, 1, None} optional
    Axis along which the sum is computed. The default is to
    compute the sum of all the array elements, returning a scalar
    (i.e., `axis` = `None`).
dtype : dtype, optional
    The type of the returned array and of the accumulator in which
    the elements are summed.  The dtype of `a` is used by default
    unless `a` has an integer dtype of less precision than the default
    platform integer.  In that case, if `a` is signed then the platform
    integer is used while if `a` is unsigned then an unsigned integer
    of the same precision as the platform integer is used.

    .. versionadded:: 0.18.0

out : np.matrix, optional
    Alternative output matrix in which to place the result. It must
    have the same shape as the expected output, but the type of the
    output values will be cast if necessary.

    .. versionadded:: 0.18.0

Returns
-------
sum_along_axis : np.matrix
    A matrix with the same shape as `self`, with the specified
    axis removed.

See Also
--------
numpy.matrix.sum : NumPy's implementation of 'sum' for matrices
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented in \mbox{\hyperlink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__compressed_1_1__cs__matrix_a1cce750a3f6a6af5c7379d01862c5fec}{scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+compressed.\+\_\+cs\+\_\+matrix}}, and \mbox{\hyperlink{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__dia_1_1__dia__base_a8e6e2b42b2ce10c4053c773edfb7f173}{scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+dia.\+\_\+dia\+\_\+base}}.

\Hypertarget{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a738fa20f9f0afdd281022da86af90855}\index{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}!toarray@{toarray}}
\index{toarray@{toarray}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{toarray()}{toarray()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a738fa20f9f0afdd281022da86af90855} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+toarray (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{order}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{out}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return a dense ndarray representation of this sparse array.

Parameters
----------
order : {'C', 'F'}, optional
    Whether to store multidimensional data in C (row-major)
    or Fortran (column-major) order in memory. The default
    is 'None', which provides no ordering guarantees.
    Cannot be specified in conjunction with the `out`
    argument.

out : ndarray, 2-D, optional
    If specified, uses this array as the output buffer
    instead of allocating a new array to return. The provided
    array must have the same shape and dtype as the sparse
    array on which you are calling the method. For most
    sparse types, `out` is required to be memory contiguous
    (either C or Fortran ordered).

Returns
-------
arr : ndarray, 2-D
    An array with the same shape and containing the same
    data represented by the sparse array, with the requested
    memory order. If `out` was passed, the same object is
    returned after being modified in-place to contain the
    appropriate values.
\end{DoxyVerb}

scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+tobsr (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{blocksize}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{copy}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Convert this array to Block Sparse Row format.

With copy=False, the data/indices may be shared between this array and
the resultant bsr_array.

When blocksize=(R, C) is provided, it will be used for construction of
the bsr_array.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\index{todense@{todense}!scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase@{scipy.sparse.\_base.\_spbase}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{todense()}{todense()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classscipy_1_1sparse_1_1__base_1_1__spbase_a1140ca1bf702cd60e263a29a8a012be9} 
scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+todense (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{order}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{out}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return a dense matrix representation of this sparse array.

Parameters
----------
order : {'C', 'F'}, optional
    Whether to store multi-dimensional data in C (row-major)
    or Fortran (column-major) order in memory. The default
    is 'None', which provides no ordering guarantees.
    Cannot be specified in conjunction with the `out`
    argument.

out : ndarray, 2-D, optional
    If specified, uses this array (or `numpy.matrix`) as the
    output buffer instead of allocating a new array to
    return. The provided array must have the same shape and
    dtype as the sparse array on which you are calling the
    method.

Returns
-------
arr : numpy.matrix, 2-D
    A NumPy matrix object with the same shape and containing
    the same data represented by the sparse array, with the
    requested memory order. If `out` was passed and was an
    array (rather than a `numpy.matrix`), it will be filled
    with the appropriate values and returned wrapped in a
    `numpy.matrix` object that shares the same memory.
\end{DoxyVerb}

scipy.\+sparse.\+\_\+base.\+\_\+spbase.\+transpose (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{axes}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{copy}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Reverses the dimensions of the sparse array.

Parameters
----------
axes : None, optional
    This argument is in the signature *solely* for NumPy
    compatibility reasons. Do not pass in anything except
    for the default value.
copy : bool, optional
    Indicates whether or not attributes of `self` should be
    copied whenever possible. The degree to which attributes
    are copied varies depending on the type of sparse array
    being used.

Returns
-------
p : `self` with the dimensions reversed.

See Also
--------
numpy.transpose : NumPy's implementation of 'transpose' for ndarrays
\end{DoxyVerb}
